## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (population dynamics / growth ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate depending on time t and current population size P, which is the standard setup for continuous-time population dynamics modeled by ordinary differential equations with density dependence and time-varying forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Constant immigration/emigration: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (baseline influx plus proportional growth/decline)
- Power-law (allometric) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (nonlinear per-capita scaling with abundance)
- Logistic growth (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (linear density dependence via carrying capacity)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (nonlinear density dependence strength/shape)
- Gompertz growth (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth decreases with log of size)
- Allee effect (weak/strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (low-density depression plus crowding limit)
- Saturating density limitation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P / (P + c2)) (crowding effect saturates at high P)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (removal independent of P, e.g., quotas)
- Proportional harvesting/mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (per-capita removals, predation/mortality)
- Nonlinear harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P**c3 (effort or predation with nonlinear dependence)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P * (1 - c4 * P) (time-periodic environment affecting r)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP_dt is approximately proportional to P across all P, use density-independent growth: c0 * P (constant per-capita rate).
- If per-capita growth (dP_dt / P) decreases roughly linearly with P, use logistic ODE: c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P).
- If per-capita growth declines slowly at first then steeply (or vice versa), use theta-logistic: exponent c2 shapes crowding nonlinearity.
- If per-capita growth decreases approximately linearly with log(P), use Gompertz form: c0 * P * log(c1 / P).
- If growth is negative at low P but positive at intermediate P (depensation), include an Allee factor like (c1 * P - 1).
- If high-P crowding effects saturate (limitation does not keep strengthening), use a rational saturation in the density term such as P/(P+c2).
- If trajectories show persistent periodic modulation in growth not explained by P alone, include seasonal forcing via sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) in the coefficient of P.
- If growth curves are systematically shifted downward by a near-constant amount, add constant-yield removal term -c2; if the shift scales with P, use -c2 * P.

Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed function):
\[
0.8770002846\,P\sin(0.5671736066\,t)\;+\;0.7013915187(1-P/65.75413114)P
\]
Expand the polynomial part:
\[
0.7013915187\,P\;-\;\frac{0.7013915187}{65.75413114}P^2
\]
So GT has exactly three components: a \(P\sin(\omega t)\) term (no phase shift), a linear \(P\) term, and a quadratic \(-kP^2\) term, and **no constants**, no other \(t\)-dependence, no logs/exp, no rational-in-\(P\), no higher powers.

Let \(\omega=0.5671736066\), \(A=0.8770002846\), \(b=0.7013915187\), and \(a=-0.7013915187/65.75413114\).

### 1.
\(P^2c0 + P^2c1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+Pc5\sin(c2 t+c3)\).
Has a \(P^2\sin(\cdot)\) term unless \(c1=0\). Then becomes \(P^2c0+Pc4+Pc5\sin(c2 t+c3)\), which can match GT by choosing \(c0=a,\;c4=b,\;c5=A,\;c2=\omega,\;c3=0\). **Matches.**

### 2.
\(P^2c0+P^2c1+Pc2+Pc3\sin(c4+c5 t)+Pc6\).
Combine polynomial: \(P^2(c0+c1)+P(c2+c6)+Pc3\sin(c4+c5 t)\). Choose \(c0+c1=a\), \(c2+c6=b\), \(c3=A\), \(c5=\omega\), \(c4=0\). **Matches.**

### 3.
\(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(c2+c3 t)+Pc4\).
Directly same structure. Set \(c0=a,\;c4=b,\;c1=A,\;c3=\omega,\;c2=0\). **Matches.**

### 4.
\(Pc0\sin(c1 t+c2)+Pc3(Pc4)^{c5}+Pc6\).
Middle term is \(P\cdot c3\cdot P^{c5}c4^{c5}= (c3c4^{c5})P^{c5+1}\). To get a \(P^2\) term need \(c5=1\). Then polynomial part is \(Pc6 + (c3c4)P^2\). Set \(c0=A,\;c1=\omega,\;c2=0,\;c6=b,\;c3c4=a\). **Matches.**

### 5.
\(P^2c0+P^2c1+Pc2\sin(c3+c4 t)+Pc5\).
Same as (3) with extra \(P^2\) coefficient freedom. Set \(c0+c1=a,\;c5=b,\;c2=A,\;c4=\omega,\;c3=0\). **Matches.**

### 6.
\(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t+c3)+Pc4+Pc5\).
Combine linear terms: \(P(c4+c5)\). Set \(c0=a,\;c4+c5=b,\;c1=A,\;c2=\omega,\;c3=0\). **Matches.**

### 7.
Has \(P^2\sin(\cdot)\) and \(P\sin(\cdot)\) plus constant \(c7\). Set \(c1=0\) to remove \(P^2\sin\), set \(c7=0\), combine the two \(P\sin\) coefficients: \(P(c5+c6)\sin(\cdot)\). Then choose \(c0=a,\;c4+c5=b,\;c5+c6=A\) (with one degree of freedom), \(c2=\omega,\;c3=0\). **Matches.**

### 8.
\(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(c2+c3 t)+Pc4+Pc5+c6\).
Must have no constant: set \(c6=0\). Then set \(c0=a,\;c4+c5=b,\;c1=A,\;c3=\omega,\;c2=0\). **Matches.**

### 9.

All terms divided by \(P+c1\); cannot equal a polynomial in \(P\) for all \(P\) unless numerator also has factor \(P+c1\) exactly, but numerator is a sum of different \(P\)-powers with sines; with free constants you could try \(c1=0\) making division by \(P\), yielding terms like \(P^2/P=P\), \(P/P=1\) etc introducing constants and losing polynomial form.
